<div id="review_371230719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/371230719" />
    <a title="Craig Slater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7405444-craig-slater"><img alt="Craig Slater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346890415p2/7405444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/371230719?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig Slater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig Slater" href="/user/show/7405444-craig-slater">Craig Slater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371230719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13589328525827730646">King of Thorns (#2 Broken Empire) by Mark Lawrence. <br/><br/>Hmm, What to say about this Author and this series, without spoiling any of the twists or surprises. Book one, Prince of Thorns was one of the surprises of 2011. If you didn't get it on your to do list you should add it now. I'll wait while you do. <br/><br/>Ok? Done? <br/><br/>At it's essence, this series is a VERY dark and violent tale, told first person, from the point of view of Jorg the young and disturbed ringleader of a brutal band of wandering misfits (Bro</span>
  <span id="freeText13589328525827730646" style="display:none">King of Thorns (#2 Broken Empire) by Mark Lawrence. <br /><br />Hmm, What to say about this Author and this series, without spoiling any of the twists or surprises. Book one, Prince of Thorns was one of the surprises of 2011. If you didn't get it on your to do list you should add it now. I'll wait while you do. <br /><br />Ok? Done? <br /><br />At it's essence, this series is a VERY dark and violent tale, told first person, from the point of view of Jorg the young and disturbed ringleader of a brutal band of wandering misfits (Brothers), that, for want of a better description, go round raping and pillaging and murdering whomever they like, and unashamedly, loving every minute of it. <br /><br />I did say it was dark. <br /><br />It's not grotesquely violent. It's not horror, but it does not 'Hollywoodize' the violence. Its real and raw. It's the Tarantino of Fantasy. The violence is somewhat confronting because Jorg is so calm about it. It's not an angry reacting to an insult. It's not vicious self defence. It’s not heroic winning after an honourable sword-fight. If that guy is annoying, or smiles oddly, and needs a dagger pushed gently into his eye, then that’s what he gets. <br /><br />It’s not all violence though. I’m just giving you fair warning that there’s some moments in there that may turn your nails black (in a good way). <br /><br />It is, in a way, the journey, both physical and mental, of Jorg, as he discovers where he came from and remembers what made him as he is. It’s actually pretty insightful. <br /><br />It could be the journey of a boy becoming a man. A man learning to control the primitive angry beast that wriggles in the shadow of many of us. <br /><br />There’s some superb humour stirred into the mix as well. I do get a big kick out of black humour. <br /><br />Mark Lawrence has a wonderful writing style, that suits this tale. <br /><br />It’s sparse and bleak. It almost misleading in it’s apparent simplicity, but then you realise he’s painting a very clear scene. <br /><br />It’s a naked grey sketch, stepping quietly along without heavy description but then he will slip in a line so masterfully crafted, so beautifully colourfully detailed, that it’s like a punch in the face with a bunch of flowers. <br /><br />The beauty stands-out all the clearer against the bleakness. The good in people stands out against all the bad that can happen. <br /><br />Maybe it’s a look at what is evil? <br /><br />Maybe it’s just Lawrence testing what we are allowed to write? <br />Many good books have tested boundaries in the past. <br /><br />Maybe Jorg is just a broken, disturbed, detached young man. <br />Maybe he’s just a cool character to write and that’s it? <br /><br />Lawrence makes you feel like a child discovering a frozen puddle on the way to school. The pure pleasure of breaking something perfect. The natural joy of not being burdened by consequence. <br /><br />Either way.<br /><br />This is a great writer and an engrossing series with a difference, not just because of its dark moments, but because of its surprising twists and revelations. <br /><br />This is a series well worth a look by fans of Fantasy, Science Fiction, Alternate History and Post Apocalyptic, or just damn good writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13589328525827730646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1547447111" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547447111" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547447111?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15765129-king-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=necromancers">necromancers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=trolls">trolls</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547447111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6810393294982536124"><b>The most interesting thing I took away from this book was that I started to like Jorg, albeit just a <i>bit</i>, more.</b> He still does reprehensible things, don't get me wrong, but he's older and wiser and not so eager to jump in and kill people without asking questions first. He strategizes a great deal more as well and really tries to think many steps ahead of his opponents. Jorg actually seems to be bothered when certain people are hurt or die, instead of just forgetting them and moving on. He thinks </span>
  <span id="freeText6810393294982536124" style="display:none"><b>The most interesting thing I took away from this book was that I started to like Jorg, albeit just a <i>bit</i>, more.</b> He still does reprehensible things, don't get me wrong, but he's older and wiser and not so eager to jump in and kill people without asking questions first. He strategizes a great deal more as well and really tries to think many steps ahead of his opponents. Jorg actually seems to be bothered when certain people are hurt or die, instead of just forgetting them and moving on. He thinks of others instead of just himself and his endgame. This book really showed a ton of growth and it felt wholly organic; it's sneaky how he makes you start to care for him.<br /><br />I made an update about Jorg's child-bride and honestly, their whole relationship couldn't have gone a better way. <b>I'm really intrigued with Miana, the twelve-year-old with more brains than many of Jorg's older Brothers.</b> There's no need to worry about her or how the marriage is handled because she can take care of herself. Sort of related, throughout most of the book interspersed here and there are pages from Katherine's journals. It was nice to have a different point of view and see what was going on with her and her family while Jorg was out conquering. <br /><br /><b>Lots and lots of questions were answered, and this entry into the series felt a bit stuffed at times, though not to the point where I thought I was being info-dumped upon.</b> We learn a lot of new things and meet more people that join up with Jorg, but thankfully many of my favorites from the first book appear here as well.<br /><br />I was kind of surprised by what happened to ... I want to say "villains" or "antagonists" but it's difficult when you've got Jorg as a main character ... so two of the men fighting against Jorg (I suppose that works) met ends I didn't see coming. It was weird but also kind of nice to not have a long drawn-out fight. And this helps me segue into my next point ...<br /><br /><b>For any gamers</b>, I've been describing this series as Dragon Age: Inquisition if your companions were assholes (tell me Sageous doesn't give you Corypheus feels with his need to mold the world to his liking, thinking he's above humanity), mixed with The Witcher 3 if Geralt was an asshole. There are a few exceptions, but that's the gist of it. In The Witcher 3 there are many times you'll do some sort of sidequest and it'll seem like it matters but it just ... doesn't. The people you meet aren't always important even though you just spent an hour or so with them. A really great article about this is: <a href="https://killscreen.com/articles/lets-talk-about-rosa-var-attre-impossible-romance-witcher-3/" rel="nofollow noopener">Let's talk about Rosa Var Attre, the impossible romance of The Witcher 3</a>. <br /><br />The two brothers that face off with Jorg don't get their time to shine, not really, and that's what made this series really come alive for me. <b>Not every encounter or fight will end up being important or meaningful or splashy with sword fights to the death.</b> Sometimes good people die and bad people win, but a lot of the time it's just not that black and white.<br /><br /><b>This series is dark and gritty but also one of the most unique fantasy worlds I've visited in a long time.</b> If you got through <i>Prince of Thorns</i>, I suggest you keep going (especially since it's only a trilogy!) because trust me, this book is a lot easier to digest.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204431300" rel="nofollow noopener">My review</a> of the first book, <i>Prince of Thorns</i><br /><br />Side-note: I know the trolls were described one way, but because of The Witcher 3 again I have a difficult time not thinking of <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YnI_mvp2fjc" rel="nofollow noopener">Trollolo</a> or <a href="https://youtu.be/KmtBSBb4hE8?t=35s" rel="nofollow noopener">Wham-a-Wham</a> or any of the other hilarious trolls you encounter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6810393294982536124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097247223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13261109314372706967">I don't want to be harsh and all, but all I can say of King of Thorns would be that it was <i> fucking </i> boring. It's a shame compared to Prince of Thorns. <br/><br/>The plot's utterly full of useless shit. This novel could've been way shorter. It has 500+ pages (on my iPad) and most of the novel was full of useless conversations. It also has too much adjectives, and tends to describe things longer than it should. And where the fuck is the action? I really liked the first book because it was full of violence </span>
  <span id="freeText13261109314372706967" style="display:none">I don't want to be harsh and all, but all I can say of King of Thorns would be that it was <i> fucking </i> boring. It's a shame compared to Prince of Thorns. <br /><br />The plot's utterly full of useless shit. This novel could've been way shorter. It has 500+ pages (on my iPad) and most of the novel was full of useless conversations. It also has too much adjectives, and tends to describe things longer than it should. And where the fuck is the action? I really liked the first book because it was full of violence and character building. This is probably the most disappointing book I've read for 2014. There are some actions in the latter part, but they aren't as exciting as the ones in the first book.<br /><br />The reason why I didn't give this the unforgiving one? Jorg. Despite the terrible plot, he's still one of my favorite characters in the fantasy genre. I might've been bored, but I still wanted to know what would happen to him. Katherine was equally as interesting as Jorg in this novel, but aside from the two, I have nothing good to say about this novel. The two got me to continue reading, but the ending's just bad. <br /><br />I didn't like the <i> dual timelines </i> going on. He could've just written all the events of <i> four years earlier </i> and then introduced <i> Wedding Day </i>. This is probably a personal preference of mine though. It's clearly opinionated but it really contributed to me disliking this novel by a great extent.<br /><br />One more thing I <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> hated would be the word fecking. It's so <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> annoying. It's not something people would want to <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> use and hear. Just stick with <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> cause you're <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> cursing anyway. A <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> child would know that fecking is just an alternative for <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i>. I just hate that<i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> word so much. <br /><br />I'm aware that almost all of my friends liked this a lot, but it just wasn't for me. I didn't like the story, and I'm not planning on reading the third book. It might be just me though, because I was really looking for great action. Although I also can't blame myself, because the first novel was amazingly action-packed. I'm just terribly disappointed. I wasted my time finishing this, because the ending was not even good. It was horrible.<br /><br />2/5 stars, because the plot is just unforgivable. Boring to a great extent, and I don't think I'll be reading the sequel to this. I just don't see any reason to do so, because I didn't like this book one bit. I <i>
  <b> fucking </b>
</i> hated it.</span>

<div id="review_1279245513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1279245513" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1279245513?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1279245513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1276714262948829222">This second book in the Broken Empire series was of a similar quality to the first. Which means it was pretty good! <br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/><br/>This story picks up 4 years after the end of the first book. An 18 year old Jorg now sits on the throne of Renar, but still dreams of being Emperor. His main competition for the role, the beloved Prince of Arrow, marches on Jorg's kingdom with an army many times that of Renar. In a fair fight there would only be one winner. Fighting fair has never been part of Honorous Jor</span>
  <span id="freeText1276714262948829222" style="display:none">This second book in the Broken Empire series was of a similar quality to the first. Which means it was pretty good! <br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br /><br />This story picks up 4 years after the end of the first book. An 18 year old Jorg now sits on the throne of Renar, but still dreams of being Emperor. His main competition for the role, the beloved Prince of Arrow, marches on Jorg's kingdom with an army many times that of Renar. In a fair fight there would only be one winner. Fighting fair has never been part of Honorous Jorg Ancrath's make up. He is a guy who will stop at nothing to achieve his ambitions!<br /><br />Like the first book this story bounced between the present and the past. In the present Jorg is gearing up for a battle with the forces of Arrow. In the flashbacks we learn of his early time learning to rule in Renar and of his journeys to seek allies and help in his bid for the empire throne. <br /><br /><b>Thoughts</b><br /><br />I liked a number of things about this second installment. The thing I liked most was the fact that Jorg showed real growth as a character over the course of the story. He is still the same old Jorg in many ways, but he is no longer driven simply by an all consuming need for vengeance. He continues to to be a compelling narrator despite his ruthless and murderous ways mainly because he can be so witty and charming. <br /><br />I enjoyed the time spent in Renar and was equally as interested in the tales from Jorg's travels. The highlight being his trip to meet with his mothers family. Jorg is twisted, but never dull. As an added bonus we also got a glimpse of things through Kathrine's eyes as Jorg discovered her diary. <br /><br />The fantasy world of The Broken Empire is a fascinating one and I was delighted we learned a few more of its secrets. I love the mix of magic and old Builder technology. <br /><br />The time jumping was not quite as smooth as it was in the first book and a few times it lead to a bit of confusion. I would have been quite annoyed if it had not turned out to be an interesting plot device of Mark Lawrence's own making. <br /><br />The story was compelling and every bit as dark as the first book. I'm fast becoming quite attached to this series. <br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: James Clamp was the narrator, as he was for the first book, and on the whole he did a good job. My main criticism is that he read this one a bit too fast.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1276714262948829222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_734092353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/734092353" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/734092353?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734092353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14909144427171304812">THE SOCIOPATH IS AT IT AGAIN While I despised Jorg in Prince of Thorns, the story itself was highly entertaining and kept me turning pages as quickly as I could read them.  However, I did not find this novel as engrossing, perhaps because I've grown somewhat use to the main character's sociopathic behavior. <br/> <br/>In any event, since the "shock" value of Jorg didn't overwhelm me this go round, I found myself focusing a great deal on the story itself, which quite honestly was a bit underwhelming.  I co</span>
  <span id="freeText14909144427171304812" style="display:none">THE SOCIOPATH IS AT IT AGAIN While I despised Jorg in Prince of Thorns, the story itself was highly entertaining and kept me turning pages as quickly as I could read them.  However, I did not find this novel as engrossing, perhaps because I've grown somewhat use to the main character's sociopathic behavior. <br /> <br />In any event, since the "shock" value of Jorg didn't overwhelm me this go round, I found myself focusing a great deal on the story itself, which quite honestly was a bit underwhelming.  I could write a multi page review about everything I disliked about this book, but in short, the storytelling was lacking, the character growth was non-existent, the plot had glaring holes, and Mr. Lawrence continued his trend of what I like to call:  the superpower of the day solution to problems.<br /> <br />Please allow me to explain.<br /> <br />In the first book and now the second, Mr. Lawrence writes our favorite sociopath into situations where no reasonable person can expect success.  Things look really grim for Jorg many times.  However, whenever he needs it, Jorg miraculously discovers some new superpower (magic, science, math, or whatever) to save his ass.  To be specific, in Prince of Thorns, Jorg was given necromancer power that kept him alive when a normal man would have died.  In King of Thorns, Jorg gets new, updated necromancer powers, fire-magic skill and Builder tools exactly when he needs them to SAVE HIS ASS YET AGAIN! <br /> <br />Of course, the negative issues with those powers - as shown clearly by their affect on other characters in the novels - miraculously leave Jorg unaffected.  And don't even bother to ask how he actually gets a thousand year old Builder's tool in book two, or how a thousand year old tool would still even work.  Who knows, because Mr. Lawrence never tells the reader either of those things.  Just poof, Jorg has this thousand year old tool, and it works and SAVES HIS ASS AGAIN!<br /> <br />Damn, it is good to be Superman in a Superman comic, isn't it?<br /> <br />But I digress.  <br /> <br />Like I stated earlier, I felt this story had glaring holes in the plot.  They ranged from unexplained entities controlling everyone to Jorg traveling to seek a fire-mage for no apparent reason to the sheer unbelievability of the battle for Renar and finally the impossible ending.  Honestly, I cannot thing of a single thing in the novel which did not just leap out at me as unbelievable and obviously yet another way for Jorg to be provided with a new "superpower." <br /> <br />Now, Mr. Lawrence attempted to minimize these problems, glossed over them as much as possible, and his usual method appearred to be mayhem or gore whenever the story was not really working.   However, this time around all the blood and brains Mr. Lawrence splatters across your reading eyes doesn't conceal that this story is not making any sense at this point.  Because, unfortunately, too much of King of Thorns is isolated incidents of horrendous gore or ghostly undead or sociopathic musings without any of it coalescing into a coherent story. <br /> <br />Another major issue in this novel was the format, specifically the flashback chapters.  I loved the whole flashback concept in Prince of Thorns, as I experienced Jorg's sociopathic behavior played out in present day yet was able to slowly understand how he reached this depraved state when younger, but the "Four Years Earlier" chapters in this book did not work at all.  Indeed, the flashbacks in King of Thorns merely interrupted the flow of the story when there was no need to do so, because - other than the one detail contained in the box about Jorq's new, baby brother (which honestly didn't amount to much) - nothing in the back story would have prohibited Mr. Lawrence from beginning at the end of Prince of Thorns and detailing this next four years of Jorg's life in a linear fashion. <br /> <br />And before anyone mentions it, I do not want to hear about Sageous, because he is only trotted out a couple times in the book and is basically a non-entity - except when Mr. Lawrence wants to somehow blame him for every horrendous thing Jorg has ever done in his life.  This one, minor character is not a reason for a flashback story. <br /> <br />As for the Katherine diary chapters, they can be summed up as boring and not relevant to Jorg's tale at all.  Sorry, they did do one thing:  give Jorg unexpected help of exactly the right sort at exactly the right time to SAVE HIS SOCIOPATHIC ASS YET AGAIN!<br /> <br />Did I mention it is good to be Superman in a Superman comic? <br /> <br />Oh, I did, didn't I.  Sorry.<br /> <br />I realize most fantasy fans absolutely adore this book.  It is hailed as the best thing since sliced bread or the internet or whatever.  But, honestly, just like the Emperor didn't have on any clothes, King of Thorns is just an okay novel.  Sure, it is entertaining, but it really isn't more than that. <br /> <br />I suppose if you idolize Jorg, it's great fun to see him rise above impossible odds to gain his desired goal.  (Of course, you have to overlook the superpower of the day problem, but fanboys don't really care about that anyway.)  But even in fanboy land, it is obvious that this novel does not rise to the shocking brilliance of Prince of Thorns, which - even with its obvious weaknesses - grabbed hold of your throat on the first page and pulled you through its gore coated world whether you wished to follow or not. <br /> <br />And, you know, maybe it was wrong of me to expect Mr. Lawrence to write that sort of book again, because there is only so much raping/killing and other sociopathic behavior one can throw at a reader before he or she grows numb to it.  Though the sadistic torture of the innocent dog in this novel was a great try.<br /> <br />However, what I had truly hoped for in King of Thorns was some growth in Jorg's character, and for a while there, I truly believed Mr. Lawrence was providing us that.  The encounter with the ghosts of Gelleth and the trip to find his mother's family along the Horse Coast - while out of character for the Jorg portrayed in book one - seemed to hold out the promise of a maturing sociopath.  But alas, I was mistaken, because by the end we discover that Jorg's touch of humanity was all an illusion caused by a "magic" box, and now we are back to the same Superman Jorg who knows all, has all the luck, and has all the powers at just the right time with the same old, sociopathic outlook on everything.  Zero growth.  Same old same old.<br /> <br />And that stupenous post-apocylaptic setting that Mr. Lawrence teased us with in the first book.  Great idea.  Very intriguing.  Not developed at all in this novel.  There is a short bit about a holographic projection of a long dead "Builder," but even that doesn't really add anything except a vague explanation of where magic came from.  In fact, the main role of this mysterious "Builder" hologram in the story is to give Mr. Lawrence an excuse as to how Jorg finds two Builder toys to (drumroll please) SAVE HIS ASS YET AGAIN!<br /> <br />Quite frankly, this great post-apocalyptic setting is going to waste, used more as a grab bag for weapons for Jorg than anything else.  And since we are talking about this, why don't we the reader know anything about the history of this place?<br /> <br />This series is called "The Broken Empire," right?<br /> <br />Jorg Ancrath is trying to reunite it as emperor?<br /> <br />Wouldn't it be useful for a reader to actually know what Empire we are talking about, or maybe why it split apart?  Perhaps some history about the last thousand years of human existence since the big apocalypse.  I mean, we get lots of talk about ancient Greek legends or ancient philosophy but nothing about this world's history at all.<br /> <br />Are there no legends or stories about the last thousand years? <br /> <br />Guess none of that is as important as watching a sociopath murder or maim someone else.  Not nearly as entertaining I suppose.<br /> <br />I realize that as I published this criticism of the beloved sociopath Jorg that I will have offended the pride many of you have in this character.  I'll most likely get so much negative feedback that I could drown in it all and that my pride might suffer immensely.<br /> <br />A time of negative comments might come.  Bad times for me.  The fanboy universe opens up and all the haters come out to get me.  But the world holds worse things than pissed off fans, because I'm a hater too.  So, the time of haters can come.<br /> <br />It will be my time.<br /> <br />If it - and my dislike of Jorg - offends you.<br /> <br />STOP ME!<br /> <br />Damn, I do love me some Jorg quotes though.  :P<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14909144427171304812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824292531?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="samantha  (books-are-my-life20)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="samantha  (books-are-my-life20)" href="/user/show/27251572-samantha-books-are-my-life20">samantha  (books-are-my-life20)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                  <em>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824292531" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3695354425331036183">King Jorg somehow finds a way to make you root for him as a reader despite his brutality. He is bold, rash, relentless, ruthless and shameless in pursuit of power and vengeance. I love falling in love with the characters and King Jorg Ancrath. I have to say it only got better in the second installment. and now on to the next book.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1030823899" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030823899" />
    <a title="Phee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26480778-phee"><img alt="Phee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580467651p2/26480778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1030823899?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phee" href="/user/show/26480778-phee">Phee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1030823899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11744102165705511062">Well, I’m pleased to say that I am pleasantly surprised at my feelings towards this book. Upon first reading I didn’t much care for it at all. I didn’t like Jorg, I didn’t care for his brothers and I got overly confused by the different timelines in this book. Couple that with my tendency to read rather quickly and I was left rather underwhelmed. <br/>However, upon my re-read 4 years later my opinions have changed somewhat. <br/><br/>Don’t get me wrong, I still didn’t much care for Jorg’s brothers. I don’t fee</span>
  <span id="freeText11744102165705511062" style="display:none">Well, I’m pleased to say that I am pleasantly surprised at my feelings towards this book. Upon first reading I didn’t much care for it at all. I didn’t like Jorg, I didn’t care for his brothers and I got overly confused by the different timelines in this book. Couple that with my tendency to read rather quickly and I was left rather underwhelmed. <br />However, upon my re-read 4 years later my opinions have changed somewhat. <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong, I still didn’t much care for Jorg’s brothers. I don’t feel like those characters are explored anywhere near enough and they aren’t developed in the slightest. Which is a shame because some of them have hints of colour to them that I would rather enjoy to see properly. <br />I also did again struggle getting the timelines straight in my head. You’d just get in the rhythm of one timeline, either Past (4 years earlier, after the end of book one), or Present- Wedding Day. You’d have about 4 chapters of one and then the timeline would change, and then it would happen again. Not to mention other chapters that are Katherine’s diary entries interspersed throughout. <br />But I slowed down my reading speed, with the help of the audiobook. And I did get my head around it in the end. I get why it was done and the story makes a lot of sense to be told in this way. Jorg in the present is slowing reclaiming his terrible and haunting memories from the past (4 years ago) and the reader gets to slowly to see, along with Jorg, just what terrible things happened. By the end it was a rather impressive show, if a little predictable. <br /><br />Now onto the things I did like. The prose was wonderfully done. Gritty and dark just like our young Jorg. But also tender and beautiful at times. It seems odd to talk about beauty in this book but there is some present. Amongst the horrors. And there are plenty of those let me tell you. Animal cruelty and rape and killing of children. Horrible things. Some of which were hard to read, even I had to grit my teeth at some scenes. <br />As terrible as these things were they did have an important part to play in the story. It wasn’t done for shock and awe. <br /><br />I really enjoyed how much Jorg grew in this one. He is probably one of the most despicable and determined characters I have ever read about. But you do see glimpses of good in him in this one. Only the tiniest slithers of good, but good nonetheless. There were actions he took in this book that were not his choices and if he had the choice he wouldn’t have gone down that path. Don’t get me wrong he is still an asshole, a major asshole. But underneath all that darkness and cunning, there is some compassion. <br /><br />I’m looking forward to the last book in the trilogy as I have never read that one. I am uncertain as to what Jorg is going to do next. But it will surly be an interesting and probably disgusting ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11744102165705511062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer4577342391853268066">Still a nasty piece of grimdark, but I have to be honest: there are a FEW more redeeming features to our young little psychopath in this book than there were in one that came before.<br/><br/>I probably sound like that's a bad thing... right? Well... yeah. I was USED to loving to hate the little murderous sociopathic little punk. I don't want him humanized. I want him to plow over all his enemies and random bystanders who might have been within spitting distance of him. I want him to burn the world.<br/><br/>Or rat</span>
  <span id="freeText4577342391853268066" style="display:none">Still a nasty piece of grimdark, but I have to be honest: there are a FEW more redeeming features to our young little psychopath in this book than there were in one that came before.<br /><br />I probably sound like that's a bad thing... right? Well... yeah. I was USED to loving to hate the little murderous sociopathic little punk. I don't want him humanized. I want him to plow over all his enemies and random bystanders who might have been within spitting distance of him. I want him to burn the world.<br /><br />Or rather, since he ate the heart of a necromancer on a freaking whim and now he has a lich inside of him as well as a warring freaking incarnation of fire, I fully expected him to raise armies of the dead and have all the bones run around on fire, destroying all the warring kingdoms and his subjects and laugh uproariously about it.<br /><br />Seriously. I'm not even joking.<br /><br />But NOOOOOO he's sinned against almost as much as he sins and that little memory trick is really kicking my conception of him around like nobody's business.<br /><br />Suffice to say, I still love the book. Maybe I'm not quite as thrilled with the sheer, utter darkness of it, but it is definitely full of some really great moments. <br /><br />Grimdark for the win! </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284264689" />
    <a title="Myke Cole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5364177-myke-cole"><img alt="Myke Cole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442476163p2/5364177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284264689?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Myke Cole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Myke Cole" href="/user/show/5364177-myke-cole">Myke Cole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284264689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15929834331187927493">Prince of Thorns impressed the hell out of me. Jorg Ancrath is the best kind of protagonist: flawed, stumbling, sometimes evil. He's human, and has that greatest of human capacities: the ability to make mistakes, learn from them, and drag the world forward with him.<br/><br/>Jorg doesn't disappoint in the 2nd installment in the series. If anything, his sharp wit, dark perceptive humor and almost precognizant read of complex situations develops. Lawrence ups the stakes in King of Thorns, and takes a comple</span>
  <span id="freeText15929834331187927493" style="display:none">Prince of Thorns impressed the hell out of me. Jorg Ancrath is the best kind of protagonist: flawed, stumbling, sometimes evil. He's human, and has that greatest of human capacities: the ability to make mistakes, learn from them, and drag the world forward with him.<br /><br />Jorg doesn't disappoint in the 2nd installment in the series. If anything, his sharp wit, dark perceptive humor and almost precognizant read of complex situations develops. Lawrence ups the stakes in King of Thorns, and takes a complex, layered approach to his story that's more daring than book 1 of the series. It's a risky move, but one that he pulls off with grace, resulting in a book that's poignant and compelling. It tips its hat to the requisite fantasy tropes while pulling the genre in a new and exciting direction.<br /><br />Lawrence joins Brett, Rothfuss, Lynch, Martin, Novik and Mieville as one of the bravest and best new voices in fantasy. With King of Thorns, he has absolutely secured my loyalty as a reader. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15929834331187927493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1925765636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1925765636" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1925765636?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=okay-shelf">okay-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1925765636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2714810254740458661">Argh this review got deleted ! Sorry to repost guys.<br/><br/><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“We die a little every day and by degrees we’re reborn into different men, older men in the same clothes, with the same scars.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Oopsy another unpopular opinion from me *evil cackle*. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479830964ra/21242237.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Firstly I must start this review by saying this book was extremely overhyped imo. Everyone raves on about how great this book is, but to be honest it was just okay for me. I once again went into this book with high expectations as I did with Princ</span>
  <span id="freeText2714810254740458661" style="display:none">Argh this review got deleted ! Sorry to repost guys.<br><br><b>3.5/5</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“We die a little every day and by degrees we’re reborn into different men, older men in the same clothes, with the same scars.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Oopsy another unpopular opinion from me *evil cackle*. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479830964ra/21242237.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Firstly I must start this review by saying this book was extremely overhyped imo. Everyone raves on about how great this book is, but to be honest it was just okay for me. I once again went into this book with high expectations as I did with Prince of Thorns and once again I've been left wondering what all the hype was about. Hype is a very bad thing. Seriously like FUCK THE HYPE (it's misleading &amp; terrible). I don't know if it's just me but everytime I read something by Mark Lawrence, I feel the book is missing something. Please don't get me wrong Mark Lawrence is a brilliant writer and very talented, I love his no bullshit style and I think Jorg is an extremely quotable character, however some things in his books just didn't add up or were left unexplained. I won't go into details because of spoilers but that ending was fucking shit. Sorry. Why wasn't anything explained? Why does Jorg always get out of ridiculous situations? Why is it so unrealistic? Honestly I have no answers to my own questions and it's bothering me. Yep I want to swallow glass and die after this book <b>BECAUSE IT ANNOYED ME. </b>Some random ass shit happened and everything is left unexplained so I'm really confused about everything, I also hate magic systems that don't have repercussions, it's just so unrealistic. <b>For me this book has more cons then pros, but I did enjoy it. </b>The story itself lacked a lot of gore and action which the first book possessed and I found the plot kinda boring, it's basically about Jorg trying to take over an empire and anyone who stands in his way will die. Sounds awesome ? Yeah I no. But it was very mellow basically this book was Jorg looking for artefacts. ZZzzzz. However I did enjoy some components of this story, Jorg is my demented hero that I love with every inch of my black heart, seriously I feel guilty for loving him so much. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446562407i/16831583.png" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>"A Dark time comes. <br>My time.<br>If it offends you.<br>Stop Me.” </b><br>Back to the bad stuff, another major issue I had in this book, I feel this isn't a spoiler more a warning but this book did have an <b>animal torture scene. </b><br><b>Yep I got the beef about it... </b>Hollywood say "don't shoot a puppy" for a reason. I felt offended by the torture scene it was so unnecessarily disgustingly descriptive and disturbing, I felt it went abit too far, but hey when reading grimdark you want to be shocked and disgusted I just didn't imagine that type of scene and kinda really wish I didn't read it, seriously where the fuck is the eye bleach at ? this book is very unique and definitely left a huge impression on me which wasn't very good. <b>However it wasn't enough to stop me from reading this. </b> I read grim dark for a reason and that's to be shocked and to be offended. So if you don't have a hardened heart this book is definitely not for you. The plot is so intriguing, I couldn't get enough. The story is very dark and when I say dark I honestly mean it, it has basically no relief definitely lacking humour and the romance is actually FUCKED UP. This book is actually kinda scary but in an awesome way. I love having goosebumps and feeling creeped out, I think Mark Lawrence does a wonderful job of weaving together interesting and compelling ideas that have you on the edge of your seat, it has the right amount of everything (except of course animal torture, I could do without). It is pretty much the bible of badassery if it was better explained but most importantly it's realistic with grey characters and Jorg defines the word 'anti-hero'. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487559062i/22026122._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The plot is extremely complex, I must admit I was really confused at times due to the POV switching back and forth from four years earlier to present. I hate first person POV, it's a peeve. I want to secretly burn all first person POV books because i hate it. I don't know how to rate or review this book because I loved and hated it at the same time so I'm just gonna say it's average. I love Mark Lawrence's writing style, I love his beautiful sentences, I love his complex characters. I'm so taken by the interesting main character Jorg Ancarth. Seriously, I can't even cope with myself when I read about him. Some of the background characters especially Sir Makin stole my heart. He is definitely a genius when it comes to writing characters. Most of the plot was interesting, a lot of parts ending up being flat for me but it was intriguing and different.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487559062i/22026123._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>If you have read this book I recommend going to google and looking at the beautiful fan art, it is all so beautiful. The covers also give me heart eyes, I LOVE THEM.<br><br>I recommend this book to lovers of grimdark and anti-heroes. All you vegetarians and animal activist should stay away. Definitely will continue with this series but I'm not in a rush.<br><br><b>Ratings;</b><br>Prince of Thorns - 3.5/5<br>King of Thorns - 3.5/5<br><br>Total rating for the series so far - <b>7/10</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2714810254740458661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_687903407" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/687903407" />
    <a title="Mpauli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli"><img alt="Mpauli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373482375p2/8323869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687903407?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mpauli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mpauli" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli">Mpauli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_gritty-fantasy">genre_gritty-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=orga_read-in-2014">orga_read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_fantasy">genre_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=rating_4-stars">rating_4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687903407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer301077089760070457">In King of Thorns Jorg of Ancrath takes the next step on his path to power. Again author Mark Lawrence shows us the becoming of a villain and as Jorg matures the story does as well. First time readers beware, this review will most likely to contain spoilers for Prince of Thorns.<br/><br/>As in his first novel, Mark Lawrence divides the narrative into two timelines. The first timeline starts immediately after the concluding events of Prince of Thorns and shows us what Jorg and his Brothers are up to for th</span>
  <span id="freeText301077089760070457" style="display:none">In King of Thorns Jorg of Ancrath takes the next step on his path to power. Again author Mark Lawrence shows us the becoming of a villain and as Jorg matures the story does as well. First time readers beware, this review will most likely to contain spoilers for Prince of Thorns.<br /><br />As in his first novel, Mark Lawrence divides the narrative into two timelines. The first timeline starts immediately after the concluding events of Prince of Thorns and shows us what Jorg and his Brothers are up to for the next 4 years. This part roughly makes up 2/3 of the book.<br />The remaining third is set 4 years in the future on Jorg's wedding day. The festivities are disturbed by the Prince of Arrows, who brings 20,000 men to King Jorg's castle in his effort to remove Jorg from his path to become the Emperor. Jorg only has around 1,000 men himself and so he has to be very clever, if he wants to survive the day.<br /><br />The second story-line is the more griping one and it's very interesting to see the battle unfolding in its various stages.<br />The pacing in the "4 years earlier" chapters is more laid back and fills us in on a lot of details concerning the world-building and how Jorg ended up to be a target for the Prince of Arrow.<br />In addition to that we also get to see what happened to Katherine in form of occasional diary entries by her.<br /><br />Overall, although I rated both books 4 stars, I enjoyed King of Thorns a bit more than its predecessor. The writing is more mature, both timelines are interesting and I enjoyed all the little tidbits of information about the postapocalyptic elements of the world-building. I would have wished to get more information about the various magical players who manipulate the kings and princes behind their backs, but as Lawrence has at least a second trilogy planned in this world, I can see why he doesn't want to reveal too much about one of the most intriguing elements of his world.<br /><br />If you liked the first one, I'm pretty sure you'll enjoy this one as well. But if you had problems with a villain being the only main pov in Prince of Thorn, King of Thorns won't turn you around. Yes, Jorg shows a few signs of remorse and is far more conflicted about his actions, but in the end you need to realize that you are reading the story of a villain.<br />I personally thing that these books are a perfect fit for a lot of young female readers who romaticize in YA novels about the "bad boy", cause Mark Lawrence's depiction of how bad boys actually treat them might spare them a lot of heartache and abuse.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1f700dUYbcG1e+7RKiRMYkSiarxPclPAnwnymOqkl32CXGGy5s0VT6Pjtwa70GfXMEXJYq/ipTvSYpsmffTGRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wLWXrbNnvGOYGTYO5hjOk2BSP3/gz2pVkmIMNXb+P4qXFwLOgLLE7Y6Bb9l37OUmFLWcoQBfnK7fCWWL4a5usw==')})
  }

Much worse.\n\nFrom being a privileged royal child, raised by a loving mother, Jorg Ancrath has become the Prince of Thorns, a charming, immoral boy leading a grim band of outlaws in a series of raids and atrocities. The world is in chaos: violence is rife, nightmares everywhere. Jorg has the ability to master the living and the dead, but there is still one thing that puts a chill in him. Returning to his father\'s castle Jorg must confront horrors from his childhood and carve himself a future with all hands turned against him.\n\nMark Lawrence\'s debut novel tells a tale of blood and treachery, magic and brotherhood and paints a compelling and brutal, and sometimes beautiful, picture of an exceptional boy on his journey toward manhood and the throne.<\/span>\n  <a
